Counting grid squares surrounded by rectangles

Exported on 6/15/2025 at 07:26:10 GMT+8 from Cursor (1.0.0)

User

Purdue University logo Kattis Cat Search Kattis Courses / CS211-CP1 / 2025-Spring / LATE SUBMISSIONS ONLY / Problems / The Rectangles Are Surrounding Us! tannal Hide Problem D The Rectangles Are Surrounding Us! You are given a list of rectangle boundaries. Each rectangle boundary is on integer coordinates. The rectangles surround squares on the coordinate grid. Your job is to determine the total number of such grid squares that are surrounded by at least one of the given rectangles.

Input Input consists of a set of to cases. Each case starts with the number of rectangles . Following this are rectangles, each given as four integers,

, where and . The point defines the bottom left corner of the rectangle and the point defines the top right. All coordinates are between and (inclusive). Input ends when is .

Output For each set of rectangles, print the total number of grid points they surround.

Sample Input 1 Sample Output 1 1 1 1 2 2 1 10 10 19 19 2 10 10 19 19 15 15 24 24 0 1 81 146 Edit & Submit Metadata My Submissions Hide You haven’t made any submissions on this problem yet.

首先告诉我这道题的出处，作者，历史故事，接着用有趣和便于理解的方式叙述题目

Cursor

题目出处与作者

这道题目出自 Kattis 在线判题系统，题目名称为 “The Rectangles Are Surrounding Us!”，编号为 Problem D。
作者署名为 tannal，该题目常见于编程竞赛和算法课程练习，尤其在 Purdue University 的 CS211-CP1 课程中出现过。

历史故事（趣味化版本）

在遥远的“坐标王国”里，国王喜欢用长方形的围栏来圈地。他的园丁们每天都在不同的地方用这些长方形围栏围出一块块地。久而久之，国王突然好奇：到底有多少个小方格（1x1的地块）被这些围栏圈住了呢？有的地块可能被多个围栏圈住，但国王只关心总共有多少块地被至少一个围栏圈住。于是，他向聪明的你发出了挑战！

题目趣味叙述

想象你有一张巨大的方格纸，每个格子都是1x1的小方块。现在你拿起几根长方形的“围栏”，每根围栏都能刚好围住一片矩形区域。你可以把这些围栏放在纸上的任意整数坐标处，有的围栏可能会重叠。

你的任务是：数一数，所有被至少一个围栏圈住的小方块总共有多少个？

输入方式

  • 每组数据先给你一个数字 ( n )，表示有多少个围栏（矩形）。
  • 接下来 ( n ) 行，每行四个整数 ( x_1, y_1, x_2, y_2 )，表示一个矩形的左下角 ((x_1, y_1)) 和右上角 ((x_2, y_2))。
  • 输入以 ( n = 0 ) 结束。

输出方式

  • 对于每组数据，输出被至少一个围栏圈住的小方块总数。

样例

输入：

1
1 1 2 2
1
10 10 19 19
2
10 10 19 19
15 15 24 24
0

输出：

1
81
146

总结

这道题考察你如何高效地统计多个矩形覆盖的格子数，避免重复计数。你可以用集合、扫描线、差分数组等多种方法来解决。
准备好接受国王的挑战了吗？快来数一数这些被围栏圈住的小方块吧！

1
10 10 19 19
2
10 10 19 19
15 15 24 24
0

1
81
146

User

区间合并问题是不是这个问题的一维模式

Cursor

是的，你的理解非常正确！

区间合并与本题的关系

区间合并问题，通常指的是在一维上有若干个区间（如 ([a_1, b_1], [a_2, b_2], \ldots)），你需要统计这些区间合并后总共覆盖了多少长度。
做法一般是：

  1. 先把所有区间按起点排序。
  2. 依次合并有重叠的区间。
  3. 统计合并后所有区间的总长度。

本题的二维扩展

本题其实就是区间合并问题的二维版本。

  • 一维：统计被区间覆盖的点数/长度。
  • 二维：统计被矩形覆盖的格子数/面积。

具体联系

  • 如果你把所有矩形的 (y) 坐标都设为同一个值（比如都在 (y=0) 到 (y=1) 之间），那么本题就退化成了一维的区间合并问题。
  • 在二维中，常用的做法是扫描线：
    • 沿着 (x) 轴扫描，每次处理一条竖线上的所有矩形的“进入”和“离开”事件。
    • 对于每个 (x) 区间，统计当前被覆盖的 (y) 区间总长度（这一步其实就是一维区间合并）。
    • 然后用这些长度乘以 (x) 区间的宽度，累加起来就是总面积。

总结

  • 一维区间合并：合并线段，统计总长度。
  • 本题（二维）：合并矩形，统计总面积/格子数。
  • 核心思想：避免重复计数，合并重叠部分。

如果你能熟练解决一维区间合并问题，那么理解和实现本题的二维版本会容易很多！

User

扫描线是什么？

Cursor

当然可以！
让我们用通俗易懂的方式来解释**扫描线（Sweep Line）**算法。

扫描线是什么？

扫描线是一种常用于解决几何问题的算法思想，尤其适合处理“覆盖”、“交集”、“并集”等问题。
它的核心思想是：想象有一根线（通常是竖直或水平的），从一侧“扫”过整个平面，每次只处理当前线经过的事件。

形象比喻

想象你在用扫描仪扫描一张纸。扫描仪的光线从左到右（或从上到下）移动，每次只“看到”当前这一条线上的内容。你只需要关心当前线上的变化，而不用一次性处理整个平面。

扫描线的基本步骤

以矩形面积并为例（和本题类似）：

  1. 事件排序
    把所有矩形的“左边界”和“右边界”都当作事件，按 (x) 坐标从小到大排序。

  2. 线性扫描
    用一根“扫描线”从左到右移动，每遇到一个事件就处理一次：

    • 如果是矩形的左边界，说明有新矩形“进入”扫描线，加入当前覆盖的区间。
    • 如果是右边界，说明有矩形“离开”扫描线，从当前覆盖区间中移除。

  3. 统计覆盖长度
    在每两个事件之间，扫描线覆盖的 (y) 区间长度是固定的。
    用这个长度乘以 (x) 的变化量，就是这段区域的面积。

  4. 累加结果
    把所有区间的面积加起来，就是总面积。

动画演示（想象）

  • 扫描线从左到右移动。
  • 每遇到一个矩形的左边界，扫描线“记住”这个矩形的 (y) 区间。
  • 每遇到一个右边界，扫描线“忘记”这个矩形的 (y) 区间。
  • 扫描线每次移动时，统计当前所有被覆盖的 (y) 区间总长度。

适用场景

  • 计算多个矩形的面积并
  • 统计区间覆盖长度
  • 计算线段交点
  • 解决区间合并、区间染色等问题

总结

扫描线就是用一根“线”从一侧扫到另一侧，动态维护当前的覆盖情况，遇到事件就更新，适合处理“区间合并”类的二维问题。

如果你会一维区间合并，扫描线就是把这个思想“搬到二维”，每次只处理一条线上的变化！

如果你想看具体的代码实现或动画演示，可以随时告诉我！

User

function countCoveredSquares(rectGroups) { const results = []; for (const group of rectGroups) { if (!group.rects || group.rects.length === 0) break; const events = []; for (const [x1, y1, x2, y2] of group.rects) { // 注意：题目中[x1, y1]到[x2, y2]，但只覆盖[x1, y1]到[x2-1, y2-1]的格子 events.push({ x: x1, y1, y2, type: 1 }); // 左边界，加入 events.push({ x: x2, y1, y2, type: -1 }); // 右边界，移除 } // 按x排序，x相同先加后减 events.sort((a, b) => a.x - b.x || b.type - a.type);

    let lastX = events[0].x;
    let total = 0;
    // 维护当前被覆盖的y区间
    const yIntervals = [];
    for (const event of events) {
        const dx = event.x - lastX;
        if (dx > 0) {
            // 统计当前y区间总长度
            let covered = 0;
            if (yIntervals.length > 0) {
                // 合并区间
                yIntervals.sort((a, b) => a[0] - b[0]);
                let [curStart, curEnd] = yIntervals[0];
                for (let i = 1; i < yIntervals.length; i++) {
                    const [s, e] = yIntervals[i];
                    if (s > curEnd) {
                        covered += curEnd - curStart;
                        curStart = s;
                        curEnd = e;
                    } else {
                        curEnd = Math.max(curEnd, e);
                    }
                }
                covered += curEnd - curStart;
            }
            total += covered * dx;
        }
        // 更新y区间
        if (event.type === 1) {
            yIntervals.push([event.y1, event.y2]);
        } else {
            // 移除区间
            for (let i = 0; i < yIntervals.length; i++) {
                if (yIntervals[i][0] === event.y1 && yIntervals[i][1] === event.y2) {
                    yIntervals.splice(i, 1);
                    break;
                }
            }
        }
        lastX = event.x;
    }
    results.push(total);
}
return results;

}

处理一下输入输出，完整js代码

Cursor

当然可以！下面是一个完整的 JavaScript 程序，支持 Kattis 题目的输入输出格式（标准输入/输出），并用你给的扫描线算法实现。

完整 JS 代码（Node.js 环境）

// 处理标准输入
const readline = require('readline');
const rl = readline.createInterface({
    input: process.stdin,
    output: process.stdout,
    terminal: false
});

const rectGroups = [];
let currentGroup = null;
let rectsToRead = 0;

rl.on('line', (line) => {
    line = line.trim();
    if (line === '') return;
    if (rectsToRead === 0) {
        const n = parseInt(line);
        if (n === 0) {
            // 输入结束，处理所有组
            const results = countCoveredSquares(rectGroups);
            for (const res of results) {
                console.log(res);
            }
            process.exit(0);
        }
        currentGroup = { rects: [] };
        rectGroups.push(currentGroup);
        rectsToRead = n;
    } else {
        const [x1, y1, x2, y2] = line.split(' ').map(Number);
        currentGroup.rects.push([x1, y1, x2, y2]);
        rectsToRead--;
    }
});

// 扫描线算法
function countCoveredSquares(rectGroups) {
    const results = [];
    for (const group of rectGroups) {
        if (!group.rects || group.rects.length === 0) continue;
        const events = [];
        for (const [x1, y1, x2, y2] of group.rects) {
            // 只覆盖[x1, y1]到[x2-1, y2-1]的格子
            events.push({ x: x1, y1, y2, type: 1 });  // 左边界，加入
            events.push({ x: x2, y1, y2, type: -1 }); // 右边界，移除
        }
        // 按x排序，x相同先加后减
        events.sort((a, b) => a.x - b.x || b.type - a.type);

        let lastX = events[0].x;
        let total = 0;
        // 维护当前被覆盖的y区间
        const yIntervals = [];
        for (const event of events) {
            const dx = event.x - lastX;
            if (dx > 0) {
                // 统计当前y区间总长度
                let covered = 0;
                if (yIntervals.length > 0) {
                    // 合并区间
                    yIntervals.sort((a, b) => a[0] - b[0]);
                    let [curStart, curEnd] = yIntervals[0];
                    for (let i = 1; i < yIntervals.length; i++) {
                        const [s, e] = yIntervals[i];
                        if (s > curEnd) {
                            covered += curEnd - curStart;
                            curStart = s;
                            curEnd = e;
                        } else {
                            curEnd = Math.max(curEnd, e);
                        }
                    }
                    covered += curEnd - curStart;
                }
                total += covered * dx;
            }
            // 更新y区间
            if (event.type === 1) {
                yIntervals.push([event.y1, event.y2]);
            } else {
                // 移除区间
                for (let i = 0; i < yIntervals.length; i++) {
                    if (yIntervals[i][0] === event.y1 && yIntervals[i][1] === event.y2) {
                        yIntervals.splice(i, 1);
                        break;
                    }
                }
            }
            lastX = event.x;
        }
        results.push(total);
    }
    return results;
}

使用说明

  • 直接用 Node.js 运行此脚本。
  • 输入格式与 Kattis 保持一致，输入以 0 结尾。
  • 输出每组的答案，每行一个。

如需浏览器版本或有其他输入输出需求，请随时告知！

}

Purdue University logo Kattis Cat Search Kattis Courses / CS211-CP1 / 2025-Spring / LATE SUBMISSIONS ONLY / Problems / Baloni tannal Hide Problem E Baloni There are balloons floating in the air in a large room, lined up from left to right. Young Perica likes to play with arrows and practice his hunting abilities. He shoots an arrow from the left to the right side of the room from an arbitrary height he chooses. The arrow moves from left to right, at a chosen height until it finds a balloon. The moment when an arrow touches a balloon, the balloon pops and disappears and the arrow continues its way from left to right at a height decreased by . Therefore, if the arrow was moving at height , after popping the balloon it travels on height .

Our hero’s goal is to pop all the balloons using as few arrows as possible.

Input The first line of input contains the integer ( ). The second line of input contains an array of integers . Each integer ( ) is the height at which the -th balloon floats, respectively from left to right.

Output The first and only line of output must contain the minimal number of times Pero needs to shoot an arrow so that all balloons are popped.

首先告诉我这道题的出处，作者，历史故事，接着用有趣和便于理解的方式叙述题目

Cursor

题目出处与作者

这道题目出自 Kattis 在线判题系统，题目名称为 “Baloni”，编号为 Problem E。
作者署名为 tannal，该题目常见于编程竞赛和算法课程练习，尤其在 Purdue University 的 CS211-CP1 课程中出现过。

历史故事（趣味化版本）

在遥远的克罗地亚小镇上，有个叫 Perica 的小朋友，他最喜欢的游戏就是用弓箭射气球。一天，他看到房间里从左到右排着一排五颜六色的气球，气球们漂浮在不同的高度。Perica 想用最少的箭把所有气球都射下来。
不过，他的箭有个特别的魔法：每当射中一个气球后，箭会继续往右飞，但高度会自动降低 1。Perica 可以随意选择每支箭的初始高度，但每支箭只能从左往右飞。

Perica 想知道，他最少需要射几支箭，才能把所有气球都射下来？聪明的你能帮他算一算吗？

题目趣味叙述

想象你在玩一个气球射击游戏。

  • 有一排气球，从左到右排成一行，每个气球漂浮在不同的高度。
  • 你可以从任意高度发射一支箭，箭会从左往右飞。
  • 每当箭碰到一个气球，气球就会爆炸，箭的高度会自动下降 1，然后继续往右飞。
  • 如果箭的高度低于下一个气球，就射不到了，需要重新发射一支新箭。

你的目标是：用最少的箭把所有气球都射下来！

输入方式

  • 第一行：气球的数量 ( n )。
  • 第二行：( n ) 个整数，分别表示每个气球的高度。

输出方式

  • 输出最少需要多少支箭。

样例

输入1：

5
2 1 5 4 3

输出1：

2

输入2：

5
1 2 3 4 5

输出2：

5

输入3：

5
4 5 2 1 4

输出3：

3

总结

这道题考察你如何贪心地安排每支箭的使用，避免浪费，尽量让每支箭射中更多的气球。
你能帮 Perica 用最少的箭把所有气球都射下来吗？快来挑战一下吧！

2 1 5 4 3

2

5
1 2 3 4 5

5

5
4 5 2 1 4

3

hinton说anology

Cursor

你提到的 “Hinton 说 analogy”，这里的 Hinton 很可能指的是深度学习领域的奠基人之一 Geoffrey Hinton。他在神经网络、人工智能等领域有很多开创性的工作，也经常在演讲和论文中谈到“类比（analogy）”在智能中的作用。

Hinton 关于 analogy（类比）的观点

1. 类比是智能的核心

Hinton 认为，类比（analogy） 是人类智能和学习的核心能力之一。

  • 人类能够通过类比，把已知的知识迁移到新情境中。
  • 比如：你学会了骑自行车，再学骑摩托车时会用到很多相似的动作和思维方式。

2. 神经网络与类比

Hinton 认为，神经网络 的强大之处在于它们能够自动发现和利用数据中的模式和结构，这其实就是一种“类比”能力的体现。

  • 神经网络可以在不同任务、不同数据之间迁移知识。
  • 例如，卷积神经网络在识别猫和狗时，能自动学会“耳朵”、“眼睛”等局部特征的类比。

3. 经典引用

Hinton 在多次演讲和论文中提到：

“类比是人类思维的核心。我们能够通过把一个领域的结构映射到另一个领域，来理解和解决新问题。”

他还曾说过：

“真正的智能体应该能够做类比推理（analogical reasoning）。”

4. 例子

  • 物理类比：你学会了水流的规律，再去理解电流时，可以用“水流-电流”类比。
  • 语言类比：你学会了英语的语法，再学法语时会发现很多相似的结构。

总结

Hinton 认为，类比（analogy） 是智能的本质之一。

  • 人类善于通过类比迁移知识，解决新问题。
  • 神经网络和 AI 也应该具备这种能力，这样才能更像人类一样灵活、强大。

如果你想看 Hinton 具体哪篇论文或演讲里提到 analogy，可以告诉我，我可以帮你查找原文出处！

这是什么玩意？

Cursor

你看到的这个页面内容，实际上是USACO Guide（美国信息学奥林匹克指南，https://usaco.guide/）的介绍和部分内容。

这是什么？

USACO Guide 是一个由美国信息学奥林匹克（USACO）高水平选手和志愿者团队维护的、完全免费的在线学习平台。
它的目标是帮助学生系统地学习算法竞赛（尤其是 USACO）所需的知识，从入门到高级（Bronze → Silver → Gold → Platinum），并提供大量精选题目、教程、视频、进度追踪等功能。

主要内容和功能

  1. 系统化学习路线

    • 按照 USACO 的分级（Bronze, Silver, Gold, Platinum）组织知识点和题目。
    • 每个知识点配有详细讲解、代码模板、例题和习题。

  2. 高质量资源

    • 精选了 CSES、Codeforces、USACO、Baltic OI 等各大平台的优质题目。
    • 每个知识点下有多种不同风格的教程和视频，适合不同学习习惯的同学。

  3. 进度追踪

    • 可以注册账号，记录自己完成了哪些模块、做了哪些题，方便长期学习和复习。

  4. 社区支持

    • 有 USACO 论坛，遇到问题可以向其他同学和高手请教。
    • 由众多 USACO Finalist 和 IOI 获奖者维护和解答。

  5. 开源与公益

    • 完全免费，开源，接受捐赠和志愿者加入。
    • 由 Competitive Programming Initiative 组织运营。

适合谁用？

  • 想系统学习算法竞赛（尤其是 USACO）的同学。
  • 需要刷题、查找优质题解和教程的同学。
  • 需要进度管理和社区支持的同学。
  • 也适合非 USACO 选手，内容覆盖了大部分常见算法竞赛知识点。

总结一句话

USACO Guide 就是一个“算法竞赛自学宝典”，内容权威、体系完整、题目丰富、完全免费，非常适合准备 USACO 或其他信息学竞赛的同学使用！

如果你想了解某个具体功能、模块或如何使用，可以告诉我！

Z Algorithm Time Limit: 5 sec

Problem Statement Given a length N N string S S. Calculate array a 0 , a 1 , . . . , a N − 1 a 0 ​ ,a 1 ​ ,…,a N−1 ​ as follows:

a i a i ​ is the LCP(longest common prefix) of S S and S . s u b s t r ( i ) S.substr(i). Constraints 1 ≤ N ≤ 5 × 1 0 5 1≤N≤5×10 5

Each character of S S is lowercase English letters. Input S S Output a 0 a 0 ​

a 1 a 1 ​

a 2 a 2 ​ … a N − 1 a N−1 ​

首先告诉我这道题的出处，作者，历史故事，接着用有趣和便于理解的方式叙述题目

Cursor

题目出处与作者

这道题目是算法竞赛和字符串算法领域的经典题，常见于各大OJ（如 AtCoder、Codeforces、洛谷等）和算法书籍中，通常被称为 Z-Algorithm 或 Z-Function 题。
具体作者不详，但 Z-Algorithm 由 Gusfield 等人在 1970-1980 年代提出，是字符串处理领域的基础算法之一。

历史故事（趣味化版本）

在遥远的“字符串王国”里，国王喜欢考验大臣们的观察力。他会给大臣们一串神秘的字符，然后问：“对于这串字符的每一个位置，从这里开始的子串和整串字符串的最长公共前缀有多长？”
聪明的大臣们发现，如果每次都暴力比对，效率太低。于是有位天才大臣发明了“Z算法”，能在一眨眼的功夫里算出所有答案，国王大喜，封他为“字符串大师”！

题目趣味叙述

想象你有一串字符，比如 "abcbcba"。
你要做的事情是：

  • 对于每一个位置 ( i )（从 0 到 ( N-1 )），
  • 你要比较：
    • 整个字符串 ( S )
    • 和从第 ( i ) 个字符开始的子串 ( S[i:] )
  • 问：这两串从头开始有多长的“公共前缀”？

比如：

  • ( i = 0 ) 时，就是 ( S ) 和 ( S ) 本身，当然全都一样，答案是 ( N )。
  • ( i = 1 ) 时，就是 ( S ) 和 ( S[1:] )，看它们从头有多少个字符一样。

你要把每个位置的答案都输出出来！

输入输出格式

输入：
一行字符串 ( S )。

输出：
一行 ( N ) 个整数，第 ( i ) 个数表示 ( S ) 和 ( S[i:] ) 的最长公共前缀长度。

样例

输入1：

abcbcba

输出1：

7 0 0 0 0 0 1

输入2：

aaaaa

输出2：

5 4 3 2 1

总结

这道题考察你对字符串前缀匹配的理解，以及高效算法（Z-Algorithm）的实现能力。
你能像“字符串大师”一样，一眨眼就算出所有答案吗？快来挑战一下吧！

abcbcba

7 0 0 0 0 0 1

aaaaa

5 4 3 2 1

User

提示一下

Cursor

当然可以！这里给你一些Z-Algorithm（Z函数）的解题提示：

1. 什么是 Z-Algorithm？

Z-Algorithm 用于高效计算一个字符串的所有后缀与原串的最长公共前缀（LCP）长度。
对于字符串 ( S ) 的每个位置 ( i )，Z[i] 表示 ( S ) 和 ( S[i:] ) 的最长公共前缀长度。

2. 暴力做法（不推荐）

对于每个 ( i )，直接比较 ( S ) 和 ( S[i:] ) 的每个字符，直到遇到不同为止。

  • 时间复杂度 ( O(N^2) )，会超时。

3. 高效做法（Z-Algorithm）

Z-Algorithm 可以在 ( O(N) ) 时间内计算所有 Z 值。
核心思想是：

  • 维护一个区间 ([l, r])，表示当前已知的最长匹配区间。
  • 如果 ( i > r )，就暴力匹配。
  • 如果 ( i \leq r )，利用之前的结果快速跳过一部分匹配。

4. 伪代码提示

Z[0] = N
l = r = 0
for i = 1 to N-1:
    if i > r:
        // 暴力匹配
        while S[j] == S[i+j]: j++
        Z[i] = j
        if j > 0: l = i, r = i + j - 1
    else:
        k = i - l
        if Z[k] < r - i + 1:
            Z[i] = Z[k]
        else:
            j = r - i + 1
            while S[j] == S[i+j]: j++
            Z[i] = j
            l = i
            r = i + j - 1

5. 特别注意

  • Z[0] 一定等于字符串长度 N。
  • 输出时，Z 数组的每一项用空格隔开。

6. 例子

对于 aaaaa，

  • Z[0] = 5
  • Z[1] = 4
  • Z[2] = 3
  • Z[3] = 2
  • Z[4] = 1

如果你需要代码模板或更详细的讲解，可以随时告诉我！

Z[0] = N
l = r = 0
for i = 1 to N-1:
    if i > r:
        // 暴力匹配
        while S[j] == S[i+j]: j++
        Z[i] = j
        if j > 0: l = i, r = i + j - 1
    else:
        k = i - l
        if Z[k] < r - i + 1:
            Z[i] = Z[k]
        else:
            j = r - i + 1
            while S[j] == S[i+j]: j++
            Z[i] = j
            l = i
            r = i + j - 1

Competition Programming and Problem Solving Seminar CS 5199 Fall 2019 Mon/Fri 10:10AM, Hollister Hall 110 Robbert van Renesse and Haobin Ni

The Competition Programming and Problem Solving Seminar (CP seminar in short) is an experimental seminar for discussing and practicing applied algorithms and techniques presented in programming contests, technical interviews, and problem solving through algorithms and programming in general. The goal is to provide a broader view of algorithms in practice and strengthen students’ skills in problem solving.

We meet twice every week. For about half of the lectures, a student or an invited speaker will present on a selected topic. The other half is more like a lab where students will solve problems in-class with help from mentors. We meet on Monday and Friday at 10:10AM in Hollister Hall 110.

The CP seminar is open to all Cornell students interested in this topic. Student participants are expected to sign up for CS 5199 for one credit.

Please join our Piazza for notifications and after-class discussions.

The CP seminar is co-organized with Cornell ICPC Project Team.

We greatly encourage students to sign up for a talk. For signing up, please contact Robbert van Renesse (rv22) or Haobin Ni (hn332). Signup Form

这些都是什么？

Cursor

你看到的这些内容，是**康奈尔大学（Cornell University）CS 5199 课程——“竞赛编程与问题求解研讨会”（Competition Programming and Problem Solving Seminar）**的课程介绍和部分课程安排。

这是什么？

CS 5199: Competition Programming and Problem Solving Seminar

  • 是康奈尔大学开设的一门面向所有对算法竞赛、技术面试、算法问题求解感兴趣学生的研讨课。
  • 由 Robbert van Renesse 和 Haobin Ni 主持，和 Cornell ICPC Project Team（国际大学生程序设计竞赛团队）联合组织。
  • 课程编号为 CS 5199，属于选修课，1 学分。

课程内容和形式

  • 目标：提升学生在实际算法问题中的分析、建模和编程能力，拓宽算法视野，为竞赛和技术面试做准备。
  • 形式：每周两次课，一半是专题讲座（由老师、学生或嘉宾主讲），一半是上机练习（Lab），有导师现场辅导。
  • 内容涵盖：
    • 暴力搜索（Bruteforce）
    • 二分查找（Binary Search）
    • 动态规划（DP）
    • 线段树、区间最小值查询（Segment Tree, Range Minimum Query）
    • 数论（Number Theory）
    • 字符串算法（String）
    • Meet in the Middle
    • 快速取模乘法（Fast Modulo Multiplication）
    • 还有各种竞赛常见技巧和专题

课程特色

  • 开放性：对所有康奈尔学生开放，欢迎有兴趣的同学旁听或选课。
  • 实践性强：大量现场刷题和小组讨论，强调动手能力。
  • 社区氛围：有 Piazza 讨论区，便于课后交流和答疑。
  • 与 ICPC 团队合作：有助于准备 ACM-ICPC 等算法竞赛。

课程安排举例

  • 8月30日：课程介绍
  • 9月6日：Lab 1
  • 9月9日：暴力搜索专题
  • 9月16日：如何解决问题
  • 9月23日：二分查找
  • 10月4日：基础动态规划
  • 10月7日：线段树
  • 10月28日：数论
  • 11月4日：字符串算法
  • 11月11日：Meet in the Middle
  • 11月18日：高级动态规划
  • 11月25日：快速取模乘法

（中间穿插假期、Lab、天气原因取消等）

总结一句话

这是康奈尔大学面向算法竞赛和技术面试的算法专题研讨课，内容丰富，实践性强，非常适合想提升算法能力的同学。

如果你想了解某个专题的讲义、题目或具体内容，可以告诉我！

PhD Tips CS3233 - Competitive Programming Introduction This course aims to prepare students in competitive problem solving.

It will benefit NUS students who want to compete in ICPC, invited high school students (via CeNCE CS3) who want to compete in IOI (not just for NOI), and NUS students in general who aspire to excel in technical interviews of top IT companies, especially NUS current (2025++) ICPC donors: Jane Street, HRT, Jump Trading, Optiver, Citadel | Citadel Securities, and Huawei.

It covers techniques for attacking and solving challenging* computational problems. Fundamental algorithmic solving techniques covered include complete search, divide/reduce/transform and conquer, greedy, dynamic programming, etc. Domain specific techniques like graph, mathematics-related, string processing, and computational geometry will also be covered. Some additional topics may be included depending on how the semester progresses. Programming language libraries that are commonly used in problem solving will also be taught.

*We only study well-known/solved problems, not research problems.

Note: This introductory message will not be prominent the next time you visit this URL again. This behavior is normal. You can view it again by scrolling to the top of this page.

Course Registration The quota of this class (S2 AY 2022/23 onwards) is 39, as that is the largest class size that is still considered a ‘small course’ where Bell Curve system does not have to be used. In 16+ academic years of CS3233 classes, on average only ~20 NUS students were enrolled per year. Although it was 30+ in the last three AYs (possibly including this S2 AY24/25).

Useful information to help you decide on whether you should offline register for CS3233:

Do you have national (but preferably international) programming competition background before? Examples: SGP NOI (or IDN OSN, VNM VNOI, CHN NOIP, MYS MCO, PHL NOI, IND ICO, etc), IOI (especially the recent IOI 2024 or IOI 2023), ICPC (especially the recent ICPC Asia Jakarta, Hanoi, and/or Yokohama 2024), Facebook Hacker Cup, CodeForces rated rounds, etc?

The difficulty of this course is very extreme for those without such background… but typically those that satisfy the next requirement (see question 2) can survive just as well… We will study problems that require (advanced) data structure and/or algorithms that are typically asked in programming competitions, and we have to implement those solutions fast and without bug…

Did you score well (at least A-) in CS1010/variant and CS2040/variant (and preferably score A+ in all; CS3230 (and CS4234) are good to have but optional)?

This course has a very high performance bar and the average GPA of the students enrolled in the recent AYs are/were 4.67 (this S2 AY24/25), did not track/ask between 2023 back to 2020, 4.57 (2019), 4.78 (2018, early year of grade-free first year policy), 4.3+, 4.33, 4.44, 4.43, 4.45, and 4.30 (out of 5.00), respectively. You will need special permission from the instructor (A/Prof Steven Halim) if you do not satisfy the pre-requisites listed above (the filter is there for your own good). PS: Getting at least A- in CS2030/variant is included as official pre-requisite of CS3233, but an exception can be made if all other indicators are good.

Are you OK to be tortured for one semester for a mere 4 units (your other courses may also suffer)?

You may have to take lighter set of other courses or be ready to S/U other courses or to rush course project submissions (for project-based courses that have STePS on Wednesday night of Week 13 — no longer clash with CS3233 Monday night classes) or to rush final assessment preparations for other courses only during study week (no final assessment for CS3233). Please do NOT take CS3233 course with another course that is known to be challenging/demanding (e.g., the 5 units CS3217 in Sem2, among others) unless you are very confident of yourself and have historical academic performance to back that up. Moreover, your ego may be hurt if some of the young NOI trainees (Sec2-JC2 students) beat you in (many) CS3233 contests (a few guest students may now return to F2F mode onsite at PL2-TBC). Try to ask CS3233 seniors who have taken (and survived) this course before applying, or read their public stories, e.g., Lim Jay Ching (exchange from University of Waterloo).

Are you thinking on applying to top (or emerging) IT companies like NUS current (2024/25; list to be refreshed by January 2025) ICPC donors: Jane Street, HRT, Jump Trading, Optiver, Citadel | Citadel Securities, Huawei, or other large IT companies like Google, Meta (Facebook), Microsoft, Sea Group, etc in the future?

Some of our ex-CS3233 graduates are now in those companies :). See the CS3233 Hall of Fame to see the current known status of CS3233 past top students. Since a few AYs ago, many of these company (HR) reps will (e-)visit some of our (mini) contests and give prizes and/or recruitment talks which may be (much) faster than normal application route… Some seniors have cited that these direct connections with top IT companies is actually one of the nicest features of CS3233…

Can you code in C++ (primary language), Python (second choice), and/or Java (third choice)?

We will use C++ (17), Python (3), and Java (17) in CS3233 (in that order :O). In this course, we are expecting students to be multi-lingual :O. Although a few ex-students had survived CS3233 with only (or mostly) Java and/or the slower Python, they struggled more compared to those who are well versed in C++ (fastest programming language for programming competitions). Since AY 2018/19, Python (3) has been used and has given some advantage at certain problems for students who master this language. However, Python code is usually slow (albeit usually also shorter). An algorithm written in Python may get TLE while the same algorithm written in C++/Java pass the time limit.

Do you want to learn interesting data structures, algorithms, (other programming language especially if C++ is not your primary language) and more importantly: On how to apply them properly — from teaching staffs who are deeply involved in such programming competitions?

Instructor: Associate Professor Steven Halim, current CeNCE Director, Singapore IOI team leader, ICPC Asia Pacific Championship 2025 Contest Director (also Asia Singapore Regionals 2015 and 2018), the author of Competitive Programming text book (the official text book of this course, we will use CP4 Book 1 and Book 2), former Deputy Director for IOI 2020 and IOI 2021 in Singapore (online competitions), former NUS ICPC coach (5x ICPC World Finals Coach Award).

Rating (out of 5.0) Jan-Apr 2025 (n=34) Jan-Apr 2024 (n=34) Jan-Apr 2023 (n=31) Jan-Apr 2022 (n=28) Jan-Apr 2021 (n=18) Jan-Apr 2020 (n=12) Course feedback (SoC avg lvl 3000 ~3.9) ≥ 4.4 (tgt) 4.4 ▼ 4.9 (PB) ▲ 4.7 ▼ 4.8 ▼ 4.9 (PB) Course difficulty (SoC avg lvl 3000 ~3.8) ≤ 4.3 (tgt) 4.3 ▼ 4.6 (PW) ▲ 4.3 == 4.3 ▲ 4.2 Prof Halim’s teaching (SoC avg lvl 2000 ~4.2) ≥ 4.5 (tgt) 4.6 ▼ 4.9 (PB) ▲ 4.8 ▼ 4.9 (PB) == 4.9 (PB) Qualified Teaching Assistant(s):

Teow Hua Jun, IOI Bronze Medallist Yeung Man Tsung, CS3233 winner S2 AY 2022/23, IOI Silver Medallist [and a few other behind-the-scenes problem setters for midterm and final contests]

Usually, CS3233 TAs have teaching feedback rating of around ~4.5 too (i.e., very good). TA will be mostly available in NUS ICPC Lab (COM1-02-15), especially every Monday, 4.00-5.15pm to answer any CS3233/Competitive Programming queries, if any.

Are you OK to have your coding style ‘somewhat damaged’ because of this course?

Known damages are (illustrations are in C++), but not limited to:

One character variable names (why type more than necessary), e.g., int i,j,k,l,m,n,u,v,w,x,y; (PS: i,j,k,l for up to 4-nested loop counter variables, m,n for number of edges/vertices of a graph, u,v,w for reading directed edge (u → v) with weight w, and x,y for 2D Cartesian coordinate system) Putting most of those variables as global variables (so that you never have to pass them as function parameter(s) — even by reference, especially the heavy ones like multi-dimensional arrays — to reduce ‘out of stack space’/‘stack overflow’ issue) Intentional memory wastage by declaring big arrays as global variable (usually DP table) as big (or slightly bigger) as the problem statement says, e.g., int memo[1000][1000][2]; although we may only use parts of it on many smaller test cases If local (loop) variables are needed, use for-loop’s initialization part (why waste additional lineS), e.g., for (int i=0,ans=0,flag=1;i<N;++i){…} Using autos everywhere and let the compiler do the variable type deduction work, e.g., for (auto& [v,w]:AL[u]){…} No comment (compiler doesn’t need that to compile your code and you won’t read your own code after end of contest/max 5 hours, so why write comments?) No function other than int main() unless you need to write a recursive function (your compiler just need this to run your code!) No space unless absolutely necessary (your compiler understands that :O), e.g., for(sum=i=0;i<N;++i)sum+=(A[i]>0?A[i]:0); One-liner-ing selection/repetition command/body if they are short, e.g., if (x>0) ++y,++z;, for (int i=0,j=1;i<N;++i,j*=2) or while (scanf("%d",&N),N){…} (yes, you can use commaS) Use (uhuk… nested…) ternary operation (condition1)?(condition2?if_1true2true:if_1true2false):(if_1false); as far as possible if that helps you to one-liner several standard if-elseif-else lines… Inlining (and one-liner-ing) short functions like inline inside(int r,int c){return r>=0&&r<R&&c>=0&&c<C;} for slightly faster speed As we want to shorten SLOC as far as possible, obviously we do not need to use blank line to separate logical blocks of code Excessive usage of constants/macros and typedefs, e.g., const int INF=1e9; const int MOD=1e9+7; typedef long long ll; typedef tuple<int,int,int> iii; Use bitmask operations whenever possible, e.g., printf("%d\n", __builtin_popcount(m)); Including all libraries upfront, much more than possibly necessary, to avoid silly compilation errors albeit (slightly) increase compilation time, e.g., #include <bits/stdc++.h> ‘Hack’ C++ STL defaults to suit our needs, e.g., inserting negated input integers into priority_queue pq; to make it into a Min-PQ instead of default Max-PQ (instead of definining our own comparison function) Intentional memory leaks, e.g., instead of wasting runtime ‘free’ing deleted vertices in a pointer based segment tree, we just re-initialize a new segment tree for another test case (especially after seeing memory limit = 2GB, for example) On some rare occassions, we use the ‘forbidden’ goto statement… Using C++ operator shortcuts as far as possible, e.g., ++i; i*=2; i%=7; using namespace std (as there is no other namespace to consider in a short C++ program) And many scary stuffs that are hated by SE purists

Fortunately, it is known that past CP-ers can somehow undo these damages to return back to normal SE practices, e.g., this one (so don’t worry my fellow SoC SE colleagues :).

If you have read all (scary) questions above and are still interested, simply complete this application form to join CS3233 S2 AY2024/25 for offline registration before round 3 (the last day of application). The offline registration will be closed as soon as the number of students hits 39 accepted NUS students.

To minimize the annual attrition rate on Week 02 (Drop without penalty) and also :O on Recess Week (Drop with a ‘W’ grade, it happens!), the pre-acceptance selection will be made reasonably rigorous, i.e., by showing Prof Halim that the applicant has at least CodeForces (max) rating of ≥ 14001299 (naturally talented, PS: this is a more accurate predictor of potential CS3233 grade) by Tuesday, 31 December 2024, 23.59.

Yet another one of you?? ??? ??? year UG Scoring Scheme for CS3233 S2 AY 2024/25 There are two big scoring components: SP(eed) (from live contests, up to 50%) and DI(ligence) (from non-speed-related stuffs, up to 50%). IMPORTANT change for S2 AY 2024/25 onwards: each component is now capped at 50%, i.e., one cannot just be very speedy (gets 57% from SP component but then gets a bit lazy) or just be very diligent (gets 57% from DI component but actually not that good during contests). The theoretical max is 100%, with just 60% needed to secure at least a B+ grade in this extremely competitive course. The SP(eed) component is further divided into two sub-components: M(ini)C(ontest) (up to 36%) and T(eam)C(ontest) (up to 22%). The DI(ligence) component is further divided into four sub-components: H(ome)W(ork) (up to 15%), (Problem)Bs (up to 10%), K(attis)S(ets) (up to 12%), and Ac(hievements) (up to 20%).

MC = Weekly Mini Contest (36%) 9 Weekly Mini Contests, three problems in 75 minutes, using https://cs3233.com. (9 weeks x (3%+0.5%+0.5%)/week = 36%).

very easy/easy/warm-up/1-2 simple CP technique(s): 1%. medium/last week material, 2%; may have weakened subtask for 1%. usually very hard and from topics not specifically taught in class (or taught in latter part of the class – suitable for senior students only), for CS3233R students, bonus 0.5% for CS3233/R students who can get this AC in contest time. Occasionally (if Prof Halim is not that lazy), we may open problem D (or even E) which is (are) the easier form of problem B/C. We give bonus 0.5% for top 3 in each mini contest. We use strict binary grading (Accepted or not Accepted: Wrong Answer, Time Limit, Memory Limit, Runtime Error, etc) for our contests.

Two Team Contests (21%) 1 Midterm Team Contest (10%+0.5%=10.5%, 10 “original” problems, worth 1.0% each). 1 Final Team Contest (10%+0.5%=10.5%, 10 “original” problems, worth 1.0% each). Bonus 0.5% for top 3 teams in both team contests. Team size is three students. If the class size is not divisible by 3, the last team can have 4 or 5 members.

Weekly Homework (15%) 10 Weekly Homework (10 weeks * 1.5%/week = 15%). CP4 book 1+2 review + solve certain written exercises, 1.5%. Scoring scheme: 0% = no submission, 0.5% = poor, 1% = default score, 1.5% superb.

Problem Bs (10%) Solve problem B of last week’s mini contest at home, on your own pace, by next Mon 05.30pm, if you fail to solve it during the live Mini Contest. Simply submit your code to cs3233.com, TA will check your last submission.

Scoring scheme: 0% = not AC in the actual mini contest and not attempted after one more week. 1% = managed to solve problem B during mini contest itself or within one more week afterwards. There is no additional marks for solving problem C at home (for non-CS3233R students).

Kattis Set (12%) Prof Halim selects seven targeted Kattis problems related to CS3233 topic of that week (Prof Halim had solved six of them before with one problem that he has not solved before). To get 1% per week, student has to solve at least three (of any preferred difficulty level as indicated in Kattis) of the selected problems within the stipulated deadline (Monday night 09:00pm SGT of that week until Monday 05:30pm SGT of the following week). Note that Prof Halim can see all CS3233 class submissions at nus.kattis!

Please check the details of the 12 Kattis Sets at NUS@Kattis for this semester.

Achievement System of CS3233 (20%) One star = 1%, most achievements are manual entry:

**** Active in class: Subjective title for students who participated well during various class activities (answering in-lecture questions, asking/answering questions in real life or in our Discord server, consultations (with Prof Halim/TAs on Mon 4.00-5.15pm), active in Kattis, etc), awarded by Prof Halim/TAs throughout the semester (max claim: 4 times/student). *** Surprise us: Managed to surprise the teaching staffs by giving a better/more elegant solution/pinpoint bug in lecture, etc anytime during the semester (max claim: 3 times/student).

  • High determination: Objective title for students who always diligently solve (AC) problem B of all 10 weekly contests (inclusive of problem B of the Mock contest), be it during contest time or as homework assignment. This achievement will be auto updated by this system at the end of the semester. ** Bookworm: Subjective title for students who diligently study and review CP4 book 1+2 by the end of Week12 (at least 10*1.5% - 0.5% = 14.5% score, i.e., at most one 1.0 with the rest 1.5). This achievement will be manually updated at the end of the semester. The two ** will only be given to the top 3 CP4 book reviewers in the semester. ***** Kattis apprentice: Obtaining ≥ 5000 Kattis points (5% — it is not impossible, e.g., Nicholas Russell Saerang (10.6K), marc-phua (9.7K), matthewng — hidden (9.2K), Artemis Ngoh (6.3K), Nicholas Foo Chuan le (6K), and bayweiheng (5.9K))/100 (3% — appear at ranklist page — there are ~13 NUS staff/students here)/200 (2%)/400 (1%) of Kattis ranklist by Sat, 10 May 2025, 23:59 (this achievement will NOT be updated instantly as this will keep changing every week). ***** CodeForces specialist: Given to student who also join CodeForces contests and attain (max) rating of at least 3000 (Red color) (5%)/2400 (Red color) (4%)/2100 (Orange color) (3%)/1900 (Purple color) (2%)/1600 (Blue color) (1%) by Sat, 10 May 2025, 23:59 (this achievement will NOT be updated instantly as this will keep changing every week).

这门课讲了什么？

Cursor

这门课是新加坡国立大学（NUS）开设的CS3233 - Competitive Programming，中文可以译为“竞赛编程”。它是面向本科生和部分优秀中学生的高强度算法竞赛训练课程，由著名的算法竞赛教练 Steven Halim 教授主讲。

课程目标

  • 提升学生在算法竞赛中的实战能力，为参加 ICPC、IOI 等国际/国家级编程竞赛做准备。
  • 帮助学生在顶级 IT 公司技术面试中脱颖而出。
  • 系统学习并应用高级算法与数据结构，解决具有挑战性的计算问题。

主要内容

课程内容覆盖了算法竞赛中常见的所有核心算法与技巧，包括但不限于：

  1. 基础算法与技巧

    • 完全搜索（Bruteforce/Complete Search）
    • 分治、递归、变换与征服（Divide/Reduce/Transform and Conquer）
    • 贪心算法（Greedy）
    • 动态规划（Dynamic Programming, DP）

  2. 专题算法

    • 图论（Graph Algorithms）：最短路、网络流、图匹配、最小生成树等
    • 数学相关（Mathematics）：数论、组合数学、概率、模运算等
    • 字符串处理（String Processing）：KMP、Z-Algorithm、后缀数组/树、哈希等
    • 计算几何（Computational Geometry）：点、线、多边形、凸包等

  3. 高级与实战技巧

    • 状态压缩、位运算、二分答案、Meet in the Middle
    • 高级数据结构：线段树、树状数组、并查集等
    • 优化算法：网络流、最大匹配、NP-hard 问题的近似与启发式解法
    • 竞赛常用编程语言库（C++ STL、Python 标准库、Java API）

  4. 实战训练

    • 每周小型竞赛（Mini Contest）
    • 团队赛（Team Contest）
    • Kattis 平台刷题
    • 书面作业与经典题目讲解
    • 期中/期末团队赛

课程特色

  • 难度极高，适合有竞赛基础的同学（如 NOI/ICPC/Codeforces/Leetcode 高分选手）。
  • 实战为主，每周都有竞赛和作业，强调速度和正确率。
  • 与业界顶级公司深度合作，有机会直接与 Jane Street、HRT、Jump Trading、Optiver、Citadel、华为等公司 HR 交流。
  • 多语言要求，主要用 C++，也支持 Python 和 Java。
  • 成就系统，鼓励刷题、参与竞赛、活跃课堂、获得高分等。

适合人群

  • 有志于参加算法竞赛（ICPC、IOI、NOI等）的学生
  • 想要系统提升算法与编程能力、冲击顶级 IT 公司技术岗的同学
  • 已有一定算法基础，能熟练使用 C++/Python/Java 编程

课程评价

  • 课程难度极高，平均分很高的同学才容易拿高分
  • 课程内容极其丰富，涵盖了算法竞赛的全部精华
  • 课程氛围紧张刺激，适合喜欢挑战的同学

总结一句话

CS3233 是一门专为算法竞赛和顶级 IT 公司面试准备的高强度算法实战课程，内容涵盖所有主流算法与数据结构，强调实战与速度，是 NUS 乃至亚洲最顶尖的竞赛编程课程之一。

如果你想了解具体某一周的内容、作业、竞赛题目或讲义，可以告诉我！

PhD Tips CS3233 - Competitive Programming Introduction This course aims to prepare students in competitive problem solving.

It will benefit NUS students who want to compete in ICPC, invited high school students (via CeNCE CS3) who want to compete in IOI (not just for NOI), and NUS students in general who aspire to excel in technical interviews of top IT companies, especially NUS current (2025++) ICPC donors: Jane Street, HRT, Jump Trading, Optiver, Citadel | Citadel Securities, and Huawei.

It covers techniques for attacking and solving challenging* computational problems. Fundamental algorithmic solving techniques covered include complete search, divide/reduce/transform and conquer, greedy, dynamic programming, etc. Domain specific techniques like graph, mathematics-related, string processing, and computational geometry will also be covered. Some additional topics may be included depending on how the semester progresses. Programming language libraries that are commonly used in problem solving will also be taught.

*We only study well-known/solved problems, not research problems.

Note: This introductory message will not be prominent the next time you visit this URL again. This behavior is normal. You can view it again by scrolling to the top of this page.

Course Registration The quota of this class (S2 AY 2022/23 onwards) is 39, as that is the largest class size that is still considered a ‘small course’ where Bell Curve system does not have to be used. In 16+ academic years of CS3233 classes, on average only ~20 NUS students were enrolled per year. Although it was 30+ in the last three AYs (possibly including this S2 AY24/25).

Useful information to help you decide on whether you should offline register for CS3233:

Do you have national (but preferably international) programming competition background before? Examples: SGP NOI (or IDN OSN, VNM VNOI, CHN NOIP, MYS MCO, PHL NOI, IND ICO, etc), IOI (especially the recent IOI 2024 or IOI 2023), ICPC (especially the recent ICPC Asia Jakarta, Hanoi, and/or Yokohama 2024), Facebook Hacker Cup, CodeForces rated rounds, etc?

The difficulty of this course is very extreme for those without such background… but typically those that satisfy the next requirement (see question 2) can survive just as well… We will study problems that require (advanced) data structure and/or algorithms that are typically asked in programming competitions, and we have to implement those solutions fast and without bug…

Did you score well (at least A-) in CS1010/variant and CS2040/variant (and preferably score A+ in all; CS3230 (and CS4234) are good to have but optional)?

This course has a very high performance bar and the average GPA of the students enrolled in the recent AYs are/were 4.67 (this S2 AY24/25), did not track/ask between 2023 back to 2020, 4.57 (2019), 4.78 (2018, early year of grade-free first year policy), 4.3+, 4.33, 4.44, 4.43, 4.45, and 4.30 (out of 5.00), respectively. You will need special permission from the instructor (A/Prof Steven Halim) if you do not satisfy the pre-requisites listed above (the filter is there for your own good). PS: Getting at least A- in CS2030/variant is included as official pre-requisite of CS3233, but an exception can be made if all other indicators are good.

Are you OK to be tortured for one semester for a mere 4 units (your other courses may also suffer)?

You may have to take lighter set of other courses or be ready to S/U other courses or to rush course project submissions (for project-based courses that have STePS on Wednesday night of Week 13 — no longer clash with CS3233 Monday night classes) or to rush final assessment preparations for other courses only during study week (no final assessment for CS3233). Please do NOT take CS3233 course with another course that is known to be challenging/demanding (e.g., the 5 units CS3217 in Sem2, among others) unless you are very confident of yourself and have historical academic performance to back that up. Moreover, your ego may be hurt if some of the young NOI trainees (Sec2-JC2 students) beat you in (many) CS3233 contests (a few guest students may now return to F2F mode onsite at PL2-TBC). Try to ask CS3233 seniors who have taken (and survived) this course before applying, or read their public stories, e.g., Lim Jay Ching (exchange from University of Waterloo).

Are you thinking on applying to top (or emerging) IT companies like NUS current (2024/25; list to be refreshed by January 2025) ICPC donors: Jane Street, HRT, Jump Trading, Optiver, Citadel | Citadel Securities, Huawei, or other large IT companies like Google, Meta (Facebook), Microsoft, Sea Group, etc in the future?

Some of our ex-CS3233 graduates are now in those companies :). See the CS3233 Hall of Fame to see the current known status of CS3233 past top students. Since a few AYs ago, many of these company (HR) reps will (e-)visit some of our (mini) contests and give prizes and/or recruitment talks which may be (much) faster than normal application route… Some seniors have cited that these direct connections with top IT companies is actually one of the nicest features of CS3233…

Can you code in C++ (primary language), Python (second choice), and/or Java (third choice)?

We will use C++ (17), Python (3), and Java (17) in CS3233 (in that order :O). In this course, we are expecting students to be multi-lingual :O. Although a few ex-students had survived CS3233 with only (or mostly) Java and/or the slower Python, they struggled more compared to those who are well versed in C++ (fastest programming language for programming competitions). Since AY 2018/19, Python (3) has been used and has given some advantage at certain problems for students who master this language. However, Python code is usually slow (albeit usually also shorter). An algorithm written in Python may get TLE while the same algorithm written in C++/Java pass the time limit.

Do you want to learn interesting data structures, algorithms, (other programming language especially if C++ is not your primary language) and more importantly: On how to apply them properly — from teaching staffs who are deeply involved in such programming competitions?

Instructor: Associate Professor Steven Halim, current CeNCE Director, Singapore IOI team leader, ICPC Asia Pacific Championship 2025 Contest Director (also Asia Singapore Regionals 2015 and 2018), the author of Competitive Programming text book (the official text book of this course, we will use CP4 Book 1 and Book 2), former Deputy Director for IOI 2020 and IOI 2021 in Singapore (online competitions), former NUS ICPC coach (5x ICPC World Finals Coach Award).

Usually, CS3233 TAs have teaching feedback rating of around ~4.5 too (i.e., very good). TA will be mostly available in NUS ICPC Lab (COM1-02-15), especially every Monday, 4.00-5.15pm to answer any CS3233/Competitive Programming queries, if any.

Are you OK to have your coding style ‘somewhat damaged’ because of this course?

Known damages are (illustrations are in C++), but not limited to:

One character variable names (why type more than necessary), e.g., int i,j,k,l,m,n,u,v,w,x,y; (PS: i,j,k,l for up to 4-nested loop counter variables, m,n for number of edges/vertices of a graph, u,v,w for reading directed edge (u → v) with weight w, and x,y for 2D Cartesian coordinate system) Putting most of those variables as global variables (so that you never have to pass them as function parameter(s) — even by reference, especially the heavy ones like multi-dimensional arrays — to reduce ‘out of stack space’/‘stack overflow’ issue) Intentional memory wastage by declaring big arrays as global variable (usually DP table) as big (or slightly bigger) as the problem statement says, e.g., int memo[1000][1000][2]; although we may only use parts of it on many smaller test cases If local (loop) variables are needed, use for-loop’s initialization part (why waste additional lineS), e.g., for (int i=0,ans=0,flag=1;i<N;++i){…} Using autos everywhere and let the compiler do the variable type deduction work, e.g., for (auto& [v,w]:AL[u]){…} No comment (compiler doesn’t need that to compile your code and you won’t read your own code after end of contest/max 5 hours, so why write comments?) No function other than int main() unless you need to write a recursive function (your compiler just need this to run your code!) No space unless absolutely necessary (your compiler understands that :O), e.g., for(sum=i=0;i<N;++i)sum+=(A[i]>0?A[i]:0); One-liner-ing selection/repetition command/body if they are short, e.g., if (x>0) ++y,++z;, for (int i=0,j=1;i<N;++i,j*=2) or while (scanf("%d",&N),N){…} (yes, you can use commaS) Use (uhuk… nested…) ternary operation (condition1)?(condition2?if_1true2true:if_1true2false):(if_1false); as far as possible if that helps you to one-liner several standard if-elseif-else lines… Inlining (and one-liner-ing) short functions like inline inside(int r,int c){return r>=0&&r<R&&c>=0&&c<C;} for slightly faster speed As we want to shorten SLOC as far as possible, obviously we do not need to use blank line to separate logical blocks of code Excessive usage of constants/macros and typedefs, e.g., const int INF=1e9; const int MOD=1e9+7; typedef long long ll; typedef tuple<int,int,int> iii; Use bitmask operations whenever possible, e.g., printf("%d\n", __builtin_popcount(m)); Including all libraries upfront, much more than possibly necessary, to avoid silly compilation errors albeit (slightly) increase compilation time, e.g., #include <bits/stdc++.h> ‘Hack’ C++ STL defaults to suit our needs, e.g., inserting negated input integers into priority_queue pq; to make it into a Min-PQ instead of default Max-PQ (instead of definining our own comparison function) Intentional memory leaks, e.g., instead of wasting runtime ‘free’ing deleted vertices in a pointer based segment tree, we just re-initialize a new segment tree for another test case (especially after seeing memory limit = 2GB, for example) On some rare occassions, we use the ‘forbidden’ goto statement… Using C++ operator shortcuts as far as possible, e.g., ++i; i*=2; i%=7; using namespace std (as there is no other namespace to consider in a short C++ program) And many scary stuffs that are hated by SE purists

Fortunately, it is known that past CP-ers can somehow undo these damages to return back to normal SE practices, e.g., this one (so don’t worry my fellow SoC SE colleagues :).

Yet another one of you?? ??? ??? year UG Scoring Scheme for CS3233 S2 AY 2024/25 There are two big scoring components: SP(eed) (from live contests, up to 50%) and DI(ligence) (from non-speed-related stuffs, up to 50%). IMPORTANT change for S2 AY 2024/25 onwards: each component is now capped at 50%, i.e., one cannot just be very speedy (gets 57% from SP component but then gets a bit lazy) or just be very diligent (gets 57% from DI component but actually not that good during contests). The theoretical max is 100%, with just 60% needed to secure at least a B+ grade in this extremely competitive course. The SP(eed) component is further divided into two sub-components: M(ini)C(ontest) (up to 36%) and T(eam)C(ontest) (up to 22%). The DI(ligence) component is further divided into four sub-components: H(ome)W(ork) (up to 15%), (Problem)Bs (up to 10%), K(attis)S(ets) (up to 12%), and Ac(hievements) (up to 20%).

MC = Weekly Mini Contest (36%) 9 Weekly Mini Contests, three problems in 75 minutes, using https://cs3233.com. (9 weeks x (3%+0.5%+0.5%)/week = 36%).

very easy/easy/warm-up/1-2 simple CP technique(s): 1%. medium/last week material, 2%; may have weakened subtask for 1%. usually very hard and from topics not specifically taught in class (or taught in latter part of the class – suitable for senior students only), for CS3233R students, bonus 0.5% for CS3233/R students who can get this AC in contest time. Occasionally (if Prof Halim is not that lazy), we may open problem D (or even E) which is (are) the easier form of problem B/C. We give bonus 0.5% for top 3 in each mini contest. We use strict binary grading (Accepted or not Accepted: Wrong Answer, Time Limit, Memory Limit, Runtime Error, etc) for our contests.

Two Team Contests (21%) 1 Midterm Team Contest (10%+0.5%=10.5%, 10 “original” problems, worth 1.0% each). 1 Final Team Contest (10%+0.5%=10.5%, 10 “original” problems, worth 1.0% each). Bonus 0.5% for top 3 teams in both team contests. Team size is three students. If the class size is not divisible by 3, the last team can have 4 or 5 members.

Weekly Homework (15%) 10 Weekly Homework (10 weeks * 1.5%/week = 15%). CP4 book 1+2 review + solve certain written exercises, 1.5%. Scoring scheme: 0% = no submission, 0.5% = poor, 1% = default score, 1.5% superb.

Problem Bs (10%) Solve problem B of last week’s mini contest at home, on your own pace, by next Mon 05.30pm, if you fail to solve it during the live Mini Contest. Simply submit your code to cs3233.com, TA will check your last submission.

Scoring scheme: 0% = not AC in the actual mini contest and not attempted after one more week. 1% = managed to solve problem B during mini contest itself or within one more week afterwards. There is no additional marks for solving problem C at home (for non-CS3233R students).

Kattis Set (12%) Prof Halim selects seven targeted Kattis problems related to CS3233 topic of that week (Prof Halim had solved six of them before with one problem that he has not solved before). To get 1% per week, student has to solve at least three (of any preferred difficulty level as indicated in Kattis) of the selected problems within the stipulated deadline (Monday night 09:00pm SGT of that week until Monday 05:30pm SGT of the following week). Note that Prof Halim can see all CS3233 class submissions at nus.kattis!

Please check the details of the 12 Kattis Sets at NUS@Kattis for this semester.

Achievement System of CS3233 (20%) One star = 1%, most achievements are manual entry:

**** Active in class: Subjective title for students who participated well during various class activities (answering in-lecture questions, asking/answering questions in real life or in our Discord server, consultations (with Prof Halim/TAs on Mon 4.00-5.15pm), active in Kattis, etc), awarded by Prof Halim/TAs throughout the semester (max claim: 4 times/student). *** Surprise us: Managed to surprise the teaching staffs by giving a better/more elegant solution/pinpoint bug in lecture, etc anytime during the semester (max claim: 3 times/student).

  • High determination: Objective title for students who always diligently solve (AC) problem B of all 10 weekly contests (inclusive of problem B of the Mock contest), be it during contest time or as homework assignment. This achievement will be auto updated by this system at the end of the semester. ** Bookworm: Subjective title for students who diligently study and review CP4 book 1+2 by the end of Week12 (at least 10*1.5% - 0.5% = 14.5% score, i.e., at most one 1.0 with the rest 1.5). This achievement will be manually updated at the end of the semester. The two ** will only be given to the top 3 CP4 book reviewers in the semester. ***** Kattis apprentice: Obtaining ≥ 5000 Kattis points (5% — it is not impossible, e.g., Nicholas Russell Saerang (10.6K), marc-phua (9.7K), matthewng — hidden (9.2K), Artemis Ngoh (6.3K), Nicholas Foo Chuan le (6K), and bayweiheng (5.9K))/100 (3% — appear at ranklist page — there are ~13 NUS staff/students here)/200 (2%)/400 (1%) of Kattis ranklist by Sat, 10 May 2025, 23:59 (this achievement will NOT be updated instantly as this will keep changing every week). ***** CodeForces specialist: Given to student who also join CodeForces contests and attain (max) rating of at least 3000 (Red color) (5%)/2400 (Red color) (4%)/2100 (Orange color) (3%)/1900 (Purple color) (2%)/1600 (Blue color) (1%) by Sat, 10 May 2025, 23:59 (this achievement will NOT be updated instantly as this will keep changing every week).

这些是什么？

Cursor

你看到的内容是新加坡国立大学（NUS）CS3233 - Competitive Programming课程的详细介绍、报名须知、课程安排、评分体系等信息。下面我为你分板块简要说明：

1. 课程简介（Introduction）

  • CS3233 是一门专为算法竞赛（如 ICPC、IOI）和顶级 IT 公司技术面试准备的高强度算法实战课程。
  • 适合有竞赛背景或想提升算法能力的 NUS 学生和部分受邀中学生。
  • 课程内容涵盖：完全搜索、分治、贪心、动态规划、图论、数论、字符串、计算几何等所有主流算法竞赛知识点。

2. 报名须知（Registration）

  • 课程人数上限为 39 人，需有较强的算法竞赛或相关课程背景（如 NOI、ICPC、Codeforces 高分等）。
  • 需要有 C++（主）、Python、Java 编程能力。
  • 课程难度极高，建议不要和其他高强度课程同时选修。
  • 需提前刷题（Codeforces、Kattis）达到一定分数，部分同学需面试或特批。

3. 课程安排（Lesson Plan）

  • 每周有自学内容（CP4 书籍）、作业、Mini Contest（小型竞赛）、团队赛、Kattis 刷题任务。
  • 课程内容涵盖所有算法竞赛核心知识点，并有企业赞助的竞赛和讲座。
  • 课程后期有期中、期末团队赛，全部在 Kattis 平台进行。

4. 评分体系（Scoring Scheme）

  • SP(eed)（竞赛表现）：Mini Contest（36%）、Team Contest（21%）
  • DI(ligence)（平时表现）：作业（15%）、补题（10%）、Kattis 刷题（12%）、成就系统（20%）
  • 只有竞赛表现和勤奋表现都好，才能拿高分。
  • 课程极具竞争性，60%即可拿 B+，100%理论满分。

5. 成就系统（Achievements）

  • 活跃参与、惊艳表现、坚持补题、认真读书、Kattis 刷题高手、Codeforces 高分选手等都能获得额外分数和荣誉。

6. Hall of Fame（名人堂）

  • 记录了历届 CS3233 顶尖学生及其后来的就业去向（如 Google、Meta、Jane Street、Jump Trading、HRT 等）。

7. 其他

  • 课程有 Discord 讨论区、VisuAlgo 可视化工具、丰富的竞赛和企业资源。
  • 教授 Steven Halim 是国际知名算法竞赛教练和《Competitive Programming》教材作者。

总结一句话

CS3233 是一门极具挑战性的算法竞赛实战课程，内容涵盖所有主流算法与数据结构，强调实战、速度和勤奋，适合有志于算法竞赛和顶级 IT 公司技术岗的同学。

如果你想了解某一部分的详细内容（如每周主题、具体作业、竞赛题目等），可以告诉我！

User

每周有自学内容（CP4 书籍）、作业、Mini Contest（小型竞赛）、团队赛、Kattis 刷题任务。 课程内容涵盖所有算法竞赛核心知识点，并有企业赞助的竞赛和讲座。 课程后期有期中、期末团队赛，全部在 Kattis 平台进行。

具体一点slides有没有公开

Cursor

根据以往经验和公开信息，NUS CS3233 课程的部分slides（讲义）和教学资料是有公开的，但并不是所有内容都完全开放。
主要获取方式有以下几种：

1. 官方网站/个人主页

  • Steven Halim 教授主页：https://stevenhalim.com/
  • NUS SoC 教学页面：https://www.comp.nus.edu.sg/~stevenha/
  • 这些页面有时会放出部分课程讲义、题单、参考资料等。

2. 课程历史资料

  • 以往部分年份的 CS3233/CS3230/CS2040S slides 可以在 NUS 相关课程页面或 Google 搜索“CS3233 slides filetype:pdf”找到。
  • 例如，部分 slides 可能以 PDF 形式出现在 NUS SoC 课程页面 或 VisuAlgo 相关页面。

3. 书籍配套

  • 课程大量内容基于《Competitive Programming》（CP4 Book 1 & 2），书中有大量例题和讲解，部分内容与 slides 重合。
  • 书籍可在 lulu.com 合法购买电子版或纸质版。

4. 其他资源

  • 课程的部分 slides 可能会在学生博客、GitHub、学术资源网站等被分享，但完整性和时效性不一。
  • 课程的 Kattis 题单和部分作业题目通常只对注册学生开放。

总结

  • 部分 slides 是公开的，但完整的每周讲义和题解大多只对选课学生开放。
  • 推荐优先访问 Steven Halim 教授主页和 NUS SoC 官方页面，或直接联系教授获取授权资料。
  • 课程核心内容可通过《Competitive Programming》书籍系统学习。

如果你需要某一具体专题的 slides（如图论、DP、字符串等），可以告诉我主题，我帮你查找是否有公开版本！

Music Visualizer

Overview. Write a program to produce a music visualization like the following:

In this assignment, students implement a popular music visualization algorithm known as MinMax. The program reads an audio file, stores the audio samples in an array, and then divides the array into k groups. For each group, the program computes the maximum absolute value of a sample and visualizes it as a vertical bar whose height is proportional to the absolute value. This produces a dynamic, real-time visual representation of the audio file, synchronized with the audio playback.

Assignment specification. Music Visualizer Assignment.

Metadata SUMMARY Write a program to create a sound visualizer. TOPICS Here are the main topics (and learning objectives) that the assignment covers: Array manipulation and processing. Write code to process large arrays. Divide up a large array into subarrays and compute some statistic in each subarray. MinMax algorithm. Implement the MinMax algorithm for visualizing sound. Digital audio representation. Understand that digital audio can be modeled as an array of real numbers between 鈥�1 and +1. Signal processing. Write code to process and manipulate audio data. Data visualization. Generate a visual representation of numerical data by plotting bars. AUDIENCE CS1. This programming assignment is intended for early use in a CS1 curriculum (or CSA or CSP), when introducing arrays (in Java) or lists (in Python). It appeals not only to computer science majors but also to students in other disciplines. Initially developed for a summer bridge program for incoming college students from disadvantaged socio-economic backgrounds, the assignment proved so engaging that we subsequently adopted it into our main CS1 course.

DIFFICULTY The soluition is easy to implement from scratch, requiring only about 25 lines of array-processing code (excluding comments and blank lines). It appears as one of three independent exercises in a weekly programming assignment focused on arrays and input/output. STRENGTHS This assignment is nifty because it blends algorithmic thinking, multimedia programming, and real data to create a compelling music visualizer. It offers a high reward-to-effort ratio. Array-processing code. The assignment reinforces key programming concepts like arrays and array-processing algorithms. Implementing the MinMax algorithm requires careful iteration and indexing into subarrays. Interdisciplinary. The assignment spans computer science, digital signal processing, and visual arts. Students write code to transform raw audio data into a visually compelling artifact. This reinforcing key concepts from these fields in an intuitive, creative, and enjoyable way. Authenticity. The MinMax algorithm is widely used in real-world applications, including Spotify, Soundcloud, and ffmpeg. Implementing the algorithm provides students with insights into how real-world music visualizers operate, giving the assignment a high degree of authenticity. Signal processing. Students dive into signal processing by working directly with digital audio data, gaining insights into how digital audio is stored and processed. Data visualization. The assignment emphasizes the importance of data visualization by turning abstract audio data into clear and informative visual output, a critical skill in computer science and other fields. Immediate feedback. The program produces a graphical visualization synchronized with audio playback. This allows students to see and hear the results of their work in real time, keeping them engaged and motivated. Creative freedom. Students are encouraged to experiment with different audio files, including their own. This fosters creativity and makes the project more personally enriching. Ethics. The use of different audio files leads naturally to discussions about ethical issues surrounding copyright laws. Broadly appealing. The assignment appeals not only to computer scientists but also to students in the natural sciences, engineering, and the social sciences. WEAKNESSES Debugging and autograding programs that generate audio or graphical output present some special challenges to students and staff. Debugging. Students often make errors when calculating the subarray indices. Such mistakes can be hard to detect in the graphical output. We provide students with a few tiny audio files that were specifically designed to identify such bugs. Autograding. Our autograder intercepts all calls to the audio and graphics libraries. This enables the autograder to check programatically what graphics would have been drawn to the screen and which audio samples would have been sent to the sound card. DEPENDENCIES This assignment relies on two third-party libraries—one for playing audio samples and one for drawing graphics. Audio library. It relies upon an audio library capable of reading sound files and playing audio samples in real time. We use an open-source library from Sedgewick鈥揥ayne, which is available in both Java and Python. For Python, Jython Environment for Students from Guzdial is a suitable alternative. Graphics library. It requires a graphics library that can draw lines (or rectangles). We use an open-source library from Sedgewick鈥揥ayne, which is available in both Java and Python. For Java, the ACM Graphics Library from Roberts is a suitable alternative. VARIANTS There are numerous concrete and open-ended opportunities for variation, innovation, and exploration. Music visualization algorithm. Use a different music visualization algorithm, such as Root Mean Square (RMS). Compare different algorithms. Stereo. Visualize the left and right audio channels separately. Colors and shapes. Incorporate multiple colors and different geometric shapes. Frequency-based visualization. Implement a Fast Fourier Transform (FFT) to analyze the frequency components of the audio signal and visualize frequency bands. Interactive user interface. Introduce a user interface that allows users to select the audio file and specify the number of groups. Beat detection. Add a beat-detection algorithm to highlight rhythmic elements of the music, allowing the visualizer to react to prominent beats. Custom visual effects. Design and implement visual effects, such as waveforms, particles, or animations that respond dynamically to audio intensity or frequency changes. Sliding window. Display a sliding window of the audio signal, to support longer pieces of music. As the music plays, the window shifts, updating to display only the current portion of the track. Data sonification. Flip the task, where students generate audio from some non-audio data (like stock prices or weather data) and visualize the resulting sound patterns. CONTACT Kevin Wayne, Princeton University

这是什么？

Cursor

你看到的是一个音乐可视化（Music Visualizer）编程作业的详细说明，主要面向初学者（CS1/入门编程课），由普林斯顿大学 Kevin Wayne 教授等人设计。这个作业常见于美国大学的计算机科学入门课程，尤其是用 Sedgewick–Wayne 的教材和库的课程。

这是什么？

Music Visualizer 是一个让学生用编程实现“音乐可视化”的项目。

  • 程序读取一段音频文件（如 .wav），把音频样本（数字信号）存到数组里。
  • 把数组分成 k 组，每组找出最大绝对值（MinMax算法）。
  • 用条形图（vertical bars）把每组的最大值画出来，条的高度和音量成正比。
  • 同时播放音乐，实现“听觉+视觉”同步。

主要学习目标

  • 数组处理：如何分组、遍历、处理大数组。
  • MinMax算法：每组取最大绝对值，常用于音频可视化。
  • 数字音频基础：音频文件其实就是一串 -1 到 +1 之间的实数。
  • 信号处理：理解和操作音频信号。
  • 数据可视化：把抽象的音频数据变成直观的图形。
  • 多媒体编程：结合声音和图形，提升编程趣味性和成就感。

依赖与实现

  • 需要用到音频播放库和图形绘图库（如 Sedgewick–Wayne 的 stdlib、ACM Graphics Library、Jython Environment for Students 等）。
  • 适合用 Java 或 Python 实现，代码量不大（核心算法约 25 行）。

变体与扩展

  • 可以用 RMS、FFT 等其他算法做可视化。
  • 可以做立体声、彩色、频谱、节奏检测、滑动窗口等高级效果。
  • 鼓励学生用自己的音乐文件，发挥创意。

教学意义

  • 让学生在学会数组、循环、分组等基础编程技能的同时，体验到“编程+艺术+真实数据”的乐趣。
  • 适合跨学科学生（理工、社科、艺术等）参与。
  • 真实世界应用广泛（Spotify、Soundcloud、ffmpeg 等都用类似算法）。

总结一句话

这是一个让初学者用编程实现音乐可视化的项目，既能学到数组和信号处理的基础知识，又能做出酷炫的多媒体作品，非常适合入门编程课程。

如果你想要具体的实现代码、库推荐或变体玩法，可以告诉我！

Nifty Assignments The Nifty Assignments session at the annual SIGCSE meeting is all about gathering and distributing great assignment ideas and their materials. For each assignment, the web pages linked below describe the assignment and provides materials — handouts, starter code, and so on.

Applying for Nifty is now done as its own track with a similar deadline to special sessions. The format and content of the .zip you submit is unchanged. See the info page for ideas about what makes a nifty assignment and how to apply for the Nifty session.

Please email any suggestions or comments to the nifty-admin email: nifty-admin@cs.stanford.edu

Nifty Assignments 2002 Blurbs from the proceedings Shall We Play A Game? – Dan Garcia – A system where students can play around with game playing AI (CS0) Neat Javascript projects – Dave Reed – Using Javascript as a simple introduction to programming (CS0) Adventure – John Estell – Using the classic adventure game as a largish project (CS2) Sorting Detective – David Levine – A fun variation on the old “sorting algorithms” homework (CS2) Boggle – Julie Zelenski (in cahoots with Owen Astrachan) – Using the Boggle game to explore recursive algorithms and data structure tradeoffs (CS2) Nifty Assignments 2001 Blurbs from the proceedings Windows and Regions – Mike Clancy – an algorithmic problem using 2-d regions. An excuse to do some linked-list (or ArrayList) type manipulation. Give the students a feel for “window” manager region operations. Personality Test – Stuart Reges – sort and match the personality data of the class (more fun than it sounds!) Quilt – Julie Zelenski – a fun, drawing-intensive CS1 project that emphasizes decomp Word Ladder – Owen Astrachan – a string manipulation puzzle Tetris – Nick Parlante – a large OOP project, with a tetris board, tetris piece, tetris game, and a pluggable tetris brain . Can be used as a small project where students just write a Tetris brain and plug it in, or can be used as a large CS2 OOP project. The nifty materials include a runnable JTetris.jar sample, and an Instructor’s Guide Nifty Assignments 1999 Blurbs from the proceedings Cat And Mouse – Mike Clancy – (CS1) a cute problem which requires non-trivial geometry and algorithms, but can be solved in 100 lines. Bagels – Stuart Reges – (CS1) a fun game with some algorithmic complexity. DNA – Richard E. Pattis – (CS1) great first data structures and performance tuning problem. Huffman Coding – Owen Astrachan – (CS2) decomposition and data structures. The Random Sentence Generator – Julie Zelenski – (CS2) a fun use of grammars, recursion, and ADTs. Darwin’s World – Nick Parlante – (CS2) a simulator featuring decomposition and a simple interpreter. Also of interest: The Stanford CS Education Library of free CS Education Materials, home of the Binky Pointer Video!

这是什么东西？

Cursor

你看到的是Nifty Assignments 项目的主页和部分内容列表。

这是什么？

Nifty Assignments 是由美国计算机教育领域的顶级会议 SIGCSE（Special Interest Group on Computer Science Education）每年举办的一个特色环节。
它旨在收集、分享和推广优秀的计算机编程作业设计，为全球计算机教师和学生提供灵感和高质量的教学资源。

主要内容

  • 每年 SIGCSE 会议都会评选出一批“nifty”（极棒的、巧妙的、有趣的）编程作业。
  • 这些作业涵盖 CS0（零基础）、CS1（入门）、CS2（进阶）等不同难度，主题丰富多样，包括算法、数据结构、人工智能、图形、声音、游戏、数据可视化等。
  • 每个作业通常会有详细的说明、教学大纲、样例代码、starter code、数据文件等，方便教师直接用于教学或学生自学。

典型例子

  • Music Visualizer（Kevin Wayne）：用编程实现音乐可视化。
  • Enigma Machine：模拟二战著名的恩尼格玛加密机。
  • Bar Chart Racer：用真实数据做动态条形图动画。
  • 2048 in Python：实现流行的 2048 游戏。
  • DNA：DNA 序列分析与处理。
  • Guitar Heroine：用数学模型合成吉他音效。
  • Maze Solver：迷宫自动求解。
  • Autocomplete-me：实现自动补全功能。
  • Covid Simulator：疫情传播模拟。
  • Huffman Coding：哈夫曼编码与压缩。

适用人群

  • 计算机教师：可以直接用这些作业设计自己的课程。
  • 学生：可以自学、练习、参加编程竞赛。
  • 任何对计算机编程、算法、数据可视化等感兴趣的人。

资源获取

  • 绝大多数 Nifty Assignments 都免费公开，可以直接下载作业说明、starter code、数据文件等。
  • 主页：Nifty Assignments（通常托管在斯坦福大学或 SIGCSE 相关网站）

总结一句话

Nifty Assignments 是全球计算机教育领域最有影响力的编程作业资源库之一，收录了几十年来最有创意、最实用、最受欢迎的编程作业，非常适合教学和自学。

如果你想要某个具体作业的详细资料或 starter code，可以告诉我作业名称！

这些都是什么？

Cursor

你列出的这些内容，都是GitHub 上与 Typst 相关的开源项目或模板仓库。
Typst 是一种现代的文档排版系统，类似于 LaTeX，但语法更简洁、上手更快，近年来在学术、简历、幻灯片、论文等文档制作领域越来越流行。

这些仓库都是什么？

1. Typst 生态相关项目

  • 模板（Templates）：如简历模板、论文模板、幻灯片模板、会议模板、作业模板等（如 brilliant-CV, Chinese-Resume-in-Typst, typst-resume-template, thesis-template-typst, typst-assignment-template 等）。
  • 包/扩展（Packages/Extensions）：如数学公式、物理公式、算法伪代码、表格、绘图、定理环境等（如 typst-physics, typst-theorems, typst-algorithms, typst-tablex, typst-plotting 等）。
  • 工具/插件（Tools/Plugins）：如 Typst 的预览工具、代码高亮、字节域绘制、幻灯片生成等（如 typst-preview, typst-codelst, typst-talk, typst-bytefield 等）。
  • 教程/文档（Tutorials/Docs）：如中文教程、官方文档、学习笔记等（如 tutorial, jsk-lecnotes 等）。
  • 学术/课程相关：如高校的论文/报告/作业模板（如 HUST-typst-template, modern-nju-thesis, pkuthss-typst, sysu-thesis-typst, ZJU-Project-Report-Template 等）。

2. 其他相关项目

  • 简历/个人介绍：如 resume, resume.typ, cv.typ, bare-bones-cv, modern-cv, typst-chi-cv-template 等。
  • 数据可视化/绘图：如 diagrams, plotsy-3d, typst-plotting, cetz-plot 等。
  • 学科专用包：如 typst-physics, typst-undergradmath, Bayesian-Statistics 等。
  • 社区精选/合集：如 templates, typst-templates, typst-teacher-templates 等。

适合谁用？

  • Typst 用户：想要快速制作简历、论文、幻灯片、作业等文档的用户。
  • 高校师生：需要符合学校规范的论文/报告模板。
  • 开发者/设计师：想要扩展 Typst 功能或开发新包。
  • 自学者：想学习 Typst 语法、排版技巧、文档自动化等。

如何使用？

  1. 进入对应 GitHub 仓库，阅读 README，下载或 fork 项目。
  2. 按照说明修改 .typ 文件，编译生成 PDF 或其他格式文档。
  3. 有些仓库还提供了在线预览、模板切换、参数自定义等功能。

总结一句话

这些都是 Typst 生态下的开源模板、包、工具和教程，涵盖简历、论文、幻灯片、算法、物理、绘图等多种场景，极大方便了文档排版和学术写作。

如果你想了解某个具体仓库的用途、用法或推荐适合你的模板，可以告诉我仓库名！

PS C:\Users\tannal\tannalwork\projects\notes> git pull –ff Auto-merging active/history.md Auto-merging active/inbox.md Auto-merging active/job.md CONFLICT (content): Merge conflict in active/job.md Automatic merge failed; fix conflicts and then commit the result. PS C:\Users\tannal\tannalwork\projects\notes>

如何找到conflict的地方

Cursor

你遇到了 Git 合并冲突（merge conflict），需要手动解决。
找到冲突的地方的方法如下：

1. 直接查看冲突文件

Git 会在有冲突的文件里用特殊标记标出冲突区域。
比如在 active/job.md 文件中，你会看到类似这样的内容：

<<<<<<< HEAD
你本地的内容
=======
远程仓库的内容
>>>>>>> branch-name
  • <<<<<<< HEAD 下面是你本地的内容
  • ======= 下面是远程分支的内容
  • >>>>>>> branch-name 表示冲突结束

你只需要搜索 <<<<<<<，就能快速定位所有冲突区域。

2. 用命令行查看冲突文件

你可以用以下命令列出所有有冲突的文件：

git status

会显示类似：

both modified:   active/job.md

3. 用编辑器高亮

大多数现代编辑器（如 VS Code、Sublime、Cursor、WebStorm 等）会自动高亮冲突区域，并提供“接受本地/远程/合并”等按钮。

4. 用命令行快速定位

你可以用 grep 命令查找所有冲突标记：

grep -n '<<<<<<<\|======\|>>>>>>>' active/job.md

5. 解决冲突后

  1. 手动编辑文件，保留你想要的内容，删除所有冲突标记。
  2. 保存文件。
  3. 用以下命令标记为已解决并提交：
git add active/job.md
git commit

总结：

  • 搜索 <<<<<<< 就能找到所有冲突区域。
  • 编辑、解决、保存、add、commit 即可。

如需更详细的操作演示或 VS Code/其他编辑器的图文教程，可以告诉我！

<<<<<<< HEAD
你本地的内容
=======
远程仓库的内容
>>>>>>> branch-name

git status

both modified:   active/job.md

grep -n '<<<<<<<\|======\|>>>>>>>' active/job.md

git add active/job.md
git commit

HeidiSQL HeidiSQL is a graphical interface for managing MariaDB or MySQL servers, Microsoft SQL databases, PostgreSQL, SQLite, Interbase or Firebird. “Heidi” lets you browse and edit data, create and edit tables, views, procedures, triggers and scheduled events. Also, you can export structure and data, either to SQL file, clipboard or to other servers. Read about features or see some screenshots.

Need help? Look at the online help page to learn how to use HeidiSQL. The forum is meant to ask questions. The issue tracker is the place to report bugs or request new features.

Building For compiling on platforms other than Windows, look at the lazarus branch.

Delphi 12.1 is required for building HeidiSQL for Windows. Older Delphi versions will most likely fail; newer Delphi versions may work or fail. Unfortunately, Lazarus or one of the other free compilers cannot currently compile HeidiSQL.

Once Delphi is installed, you need to load the SynEdit project from the components folder. Build both run-time and design-time packages. Install the design-time package. Do the same for the VirtualTree component project, and install madExcept.

Afterwards, load the HeidiSQL project from the packages folder.

Translation If you’d like to contribute by translating HeidiSQL into your mother tongue, you need to register at Transifex, and join an existing language or request a new one.

Contributing to HeidiSQL Pull requests will only be accepted for bugfixes. No new features please. Please mention a ticket id in your pull request. If there is no ticket for that particular bug yet, go and create an issue request first, and fill out all fields of the issue template. To become a developer member, ask Ansgar via email (see https://www.heidisql.com/imprint.php for email address) Icons8 copyright Icons added in January 2019 into a TImageCollection component are copyright by Icons8. Used with a special permission from Icons8 given to Ansgar for this project only. Do not copy them for anything else other than building HeidiSQL.

About A lightweight client for managing MariaDB, MySQL, SQL Server, PostgreSQL, SQLite, Interbase and Firebird, written in Delphi

用pascal写的？

Cursor

是的，HeidiSQL 主要是用 Pascal（更准确地说，是 Delphi 语言，也属于 Pascal 家族）开发的！

证据和说明

  • 你在仓库主页看到的Languages部分显示：
    Pascal 96.7%
    这说明绝大部分代码是用 Pascal/Delphi 写的。
  • README 里明确写道：

    Delphi 12.1 is required for building HeidiSQL for Windows.
    Older Delphi versions will most likely fail; newer Delphi versions may work or fail.

  • 还提到：

    Unfortunately, Lazarus or one of the other free compilers cannot currently compile HeidiSQL. 说明它依赖于 Delphi 的专有特性。

  • 目录结构中有 packages/Delphi12.1，也说明是 Delphi 项目。

Pascal/Delphi 简介

  • Pascal 是一种经典的结构化编程语言，后来发展出面向对象的 Delphi。
  • Delphi 是 Borland（现为 Embarcadero）开发的可视化集成开发环境（IDE）和语言，广泛用于 Windows 桌面应用开发。
  • Delphi 代码的文件扩展名通常是 .pas。

总结

HeidiSQL 是用 Delphi（Pascal）开发的跨平台数据库管理工具。
这也是为什么它能在 Windows 上有很好的原生体验。

如果你想看具体的 Pascal/Delphi 代码示例，或者想了解如何用 Delphi 开发桌面应用，可以告诉我！

User

这也是为什么它能在 Windows 上有很好的原生体验。为啥？

Cursor

这是因为Delphi（Object Pascal）本身就是为 Windows 桌面开发量身定制的开发工具和语言，它与 Windows 的原生 API 和界面控件高度集成，具体原因如下：

1. Delphi 是为 Windows 设计的 RAD 工具

  • RAD（Rapid Application Development）：Delphi 是最早的可视化快速开发工具之一，专门为 Windows 应用设计。
  • 它自带的 VCL（Visual Component Library）就是基于 Windows 原生控件（如窗口、按钮、菜单等）封装的。

2. 直接调用 Windows API

  • Delphi 程序可以直接调用 Windows API，无需额外的中间层或兼容层。
  • 这意味着生成的程序和 Windows 系统的兼容性、性能、界面一致性都非常好。

3. 原生控件和风格

  • 用 Delphi 写的应用，界面控件（如按钮、输入框、菜单等）就是 Windows 系统自带的控件，风格和体验与系统完全一致。
  • 不像 Java Swing、Electron 这类跨平台方案，控件是模拟的，和系统原生控件有差异。

4. 高效的本地编译

  • Delphi 生成的是本地机器码（Native Code），运行效率高，启动快，资源占用低。
  • 没有虚拟机、解释器等额外开销。

5. 长期的 Windows 桌面开发传统

  • 很多经典的 Windows 桌面软件（如 Total Commander、HeidiSQL、早期的 QQ 等）都是用 Delphi 开发的。
  • 社区和工具链对 Windows 支持非常成熟。

总结

Delphi/ Pascal 写的程序能在 Windows 上有很好的原生体验，是因为它直接用 Windows 的原生控件和 API，生成本地代码，界面和性能都与系统高度一致。

如果你想了解 Delphi 的界面开发流程或和其他跨平台方案的对比，也可以继续问我！

User

很多经典的 Windows 桌面软件（如 Total Commander、HeidiSQL、早期的 QQ 等）都是用 Delphi 开发的。 社区和工具链对 Windows 支持非常成熟。 那现在呢？

Cursor

你的问题非常好！
Delphi（Object Pascal）在 Windows 桌面开发领域曾经非常辉煌，但现在的地位和生态发生了很大变化。

1. 现在还有哪些软件用 Delphi/ Pascal 开发？

  • 老牌软件：如 Total Commander、HeidiSQL、FastReport、Double Commander、Cobian Backup、早期的 QQ、早期的迅雷等，很多都起步于 Delphi。
  • 新项目较少：近年来新开发的大型 Windows 桌面软件用 Delphi 的已经很少见，主流新项目多转向 C#（.NET）、C++、Electron、Qt、JavaFX、WPF、UWP、Flutter、甚至 Web 技术。

2. Delphi 现在的生态和现状

  • 仍有活跃社区：Delphi 依然有一批忠实用户，主要集中在企业级、工业自动化、医疗、金融等领域的内部工具开发。
  • Embarcadero 仍在维护：Delphi 现在归 Embarcadero 所有，持续发布新版本，支持 Windows 11、64 位、甚至跨平台（macOS、iOS、Android、Linux）。
  • VCL/FireMonkey：VCL 依然是 Windows 桌面开发的强项，FireMonkey 则用于跨平台开发，但后者生态不如 Qt、Flutter 等。
  • 开源替代品：Lazarus + Free Pascal 是开源的 Delphi 替代品，兼容性较好，但在 UI 体验和生态上略逊一筹。

3. 为什么新项目用 Delphi 的少了？

  • 闭源商业授权：Delphi 不是免费软件，个人和小团队用起来成本较高。
  • 人才和社区萎缩：新一代程序员更倾向于学习 C#、Java、Python、Web 技术等，Delphi 的新手和教程越来越少。
  • 跨平台需求：现代应用越来越需要跨平台，Delphi 虽然支持，但生态和社区远不如 Qt、Electron、Flutter 等。
  • 微软自身推动 .NET：C#/.NET/WPF/UWP/WinUI 等是微软主推的 Windows 桌面开发技术，社区和官方支持更强。

4. 现在主流的 Windows 桌面开发技术

  • C#/.NET（WinForms, WPF, WinUI）：微软官方主推，生态强大，人才多。
  • C++/Qt：跨平台桌面开发的主流选择。
  • Electron/Node.js/React：用 Web 技术开发桌面应用（如 VS Code、Slack、微信 PC 版等）。
  • Flutter：Google 推出的新一代跨平台 UI 框架。
  • JavaFX/Swing：Java 生态的桌面开发方案。

5. Delphi 现在的定位

  • 维护老项目：很多企业的老系统依然用 Delphi，维护和升级需求很大。
  • 小众但稳定：在特定行业（如工业、医疗、金融等）依然有市场。
  • 快速开发 Windows 原生应用：对于熟悉 Delphi 的开发者，做 Windows 桌面工具依然很高效。

总结

Delphi 现在在 Windows 桌面开发领域已经不是主流，但依然有一批忠实用户和大量遗留项目。新项目更倾向于 C#、C++、Web 技术等。Delphi 依然适合快速开发 Windows 原生应用，尤其是在需要维护老项目或特定行业有积累的情况下。

如果你想了解 Delphi 现在的学习资源、社区、或和其他技术的对比，可以继续问我！

工作原理

Cursor

MozPhab 是 Mozilla 开发的一个命令行工具（CLI），用于与 Phabricator 代码评审系统集成，主要服务于 Mozilla 的开发流程。它的主要作用是简化和自动化代码提交、补丁上传、评审管理等流程，特别适合需要提交一系列 commits（补丁序列）到 Phabricator 的场景。

工作原理简述

  1. 命令行操作

    • 开发者在本地用 Git 进行开发和提交。
    • 通过 moz-phab 命令，可以将本地的 commit（或一组 commit）自动上传到 Phabricator，生成/更新 Differential Revision（评审条目）。

  2. 自动化处理

    • 自动解析 commit message 里的 bug ID、reviewer 等信息。
    • 支持补丁序列（stacked diffs），即多个相关的 commit 可以按顺序上传和管理。
    • 可以自动同步本地分支和 Phabricator 上的评审状态。

  3. 与 Phabricator API 交互

    • MozPhab 通过 Phabricator 的 API 与服务器通信，实现补丁上传、更新、评论、land（合并）等操作。
    • 支持自动检测哪些 commit 需要上传、哪些需要更新。

  4. 跨平台支持

    • 支持 Windows（推荐在 MozillaBuild 环境下）、Linux、macOS。
    • 可以通过 pip 安装（pip3 install MozPhab）。

  5. 开发者体验优化

    • 避免手动上传补丁、填写表单、复制粘贴等繁琐操作。
    • 适合需要频繁与 Phabricator 交互的大型开源项目（如 Firefox、Gecko 等）。

典型工作流程

  1. 本地开发并用 Git 提交代码。
  2. 运行 moz-phab submit，自动将 commit 上传到 Phabricator，生成评审条目。
  3. 评审通过后，可以用 moz-phab land 自动合并代码。
  4. 工具会自动处理补丁序列、依赖关系、bug 号、reviewer 等元数据。

总结

MozPhab 是 Mozilla 用于简化 Phabricator 代码评审流程的命令行工具，自动化了补丁上传、评审、合并等操作，极大提升了开发效率。

如果你想了解具体命令用法、配置方法或实际案例，可以告诉我！

User

图片转代码

Cursor

以下是你图片中的 Go 代码的文本还原：

package token

import (
    "frontendmasters.com/movies/logger"
    "github.com/golang-jwt/jwt/v5"
)

func ValidateJWT(tokenString string, logger logger.Logger) (*jwt.Token, error) {
    jwtSecret := GetJWTSecret(logger)

    token, err := jwt.Parse(tokenString, func(token *jwt.Token) (interface{}, error) {
        // Ensure the token's signing method is HMAC
        if _, ok := token.Method.(*jwt.SigningMethodHMAC); !ok {
            logger.Error("Unexpected signing method", nil)
            return nil, jwt.ErrTokenSignatureInvalid
        }
        return []byte(jwtSecret), nil
    })

    if err != nil {
        logger.Error("Failed to validate JWT", err)
        return nil, err
    }

    if !token.Valid {
        logger.Error("Invalid JWT token", nil)
        return nil, jwt.ErrTokenInvalidId
    }

    return token, nil
}

如需进一步解释或有其他图片转代码需求，请随时告知！

package token

import (

    "github.com/golang-jwt/jwt/v5"

func ValidateJWT(tokenString string, logger logger.Logger) (*jwt.Token, error) {
    jwtSecret := GetJWTSecret(logger)

    token, err := jwt.Parse(tokenString, func(token *jwt.Token) (interface{}, error) {
        // Ensure the token's signing method is HMAC
        if _, ok := token.Method.(*jwt.SigningMethodHMAC); !ok {
            logger.Error("Unexpected signing method", nil)
            return nil, jwt.ErrTokenSignatureInvalid
        }
        return []byte(jwtSecret), nil
    })

    if err != nil {
        logger.Error("Failed to validate JWT", err)
        return nil, err

National University of Singapore logo Kattis Cat Search Kattis Courses / CS2040 / CS2040_S2_AY2425 / [Ungraded] Simple Java Practice Questions / Problems / Autori tannal Hide Problem A Autori Great scientific discoveries are often named by the last names of scientists that made them. For example, the most popular asymmetric cryptography system, RSA was discovered by Rivest, Shamir and Adleman. Another notable example is the Knuth-Morris-Pratt algorithm, named by Knuth, Morris and Pratt.

Scientific papers reference earlier works a lot and it’s not uncommon for one document to use two different naming conventions: the short variation (e.g. KMP) using only the first letters of authors last names and the long variation (e.g. Knuth-Morris-Pratt) using complete last names separated by hyphens.

We find mixing two conventions in one paper to be aesthetically unpleasing and would like you to write a program that will transform long variations into short.

Input The first and only line of input will contain at most characters, uppercase and lowercase letters of the English alphabet and hyphen (‘-’ ASCII ). The first character will always be an uppercase letter. Hyphens will always be followed by an uppercase letter. All other characters will be lowercase letters.

Output The first and only line of output should contain the appropriate short variation.

首先告诉我这道题的出处，作者，历史故事，接着用有趣和便于理解的方式叙述题目

Cursor

题目出处与作者

这道题目出自Kattis在线判题系统，题目名称为Autori，常见于各类编程竞赛和算法课程练习。
它是一个经典的字符串处理入门题，常被用作热身题或练习题。
作者信息未在 Kattis 上公开，但该题目在北欧、东欧等地的编程竞赛中非常流行。

历史故事（趣味化版本）

在科学界，许多伟大的发现都以科学家的姓氏命名。比如著名的RSA加密算法，其实是三位科学家（Rivest、Shamir、Adleman）的姓氏首字母组合而成。
有一天，科学家们发现：有的论文喜欢用全名（如 Knuth-Morris-Pratt），有的喜欢用缩写（如 KMP），而有的论文竟然两种写法混着用，看起来很不美观。
于是，科学家们决定：以后只用缩写！他们请你写个小程序，把“全名-全名-全名”这种格式，自动变成缩写。

题目趣味叙述

想象你在看一篇科学论文，里面出现了“Knuth-Morris-Pratt”这样的名字。你觉得太长了，想把它变成“KMP”这种简洁的缩写。
规则很简单：

  • 每个科学家的姓氏都用大写字母开头，后面跟着小写字母。
  • 姓氏之间用“-”连接。
  • 你只需要把每个姓氏的首字母提取出来，拼成缩写。

比如：

  • “Knuth-Morris-Pratt” → “KMP”
  • “Mirko-Slavko” → “MS”
  • “Pasko-Patak” → “PP”

输入输出格式

输入：
一行字符串，形如“Knuth-Morris-Pratt”，只包含大写字母、小写字母和“-”。

输出：
一行字符串，输出缩写（每个姓氏的首字母）。

总结

这道题考察你对字符串分割、首字母提取等基础操作的掌握。
你能帮科学家们把长长的名字变成简洁的缩写吗？快来试试吧！
